Clause Remarks Information/Comments
All General European Countries, EN 60601-1(2006) + A1:2013
Main test report contains countries deviations (Canadian,
Japan, Korea and USA), see attachment 2.
1.3 Collateral standards The equipment has been evaluated also according to
collateral standard IEC 60601-1-6:2010 + AMD1:2013,
see attachment 3.
4.2 Risk management process RM Results are documented by the manufacturer on the
basis of ISO 14971:2007 and EN ISO 14971:2012
referring to the OD-2044 (ed.2.3) from IECEE, and are
reviewed by Nemko.
4.8 Components The power supply box, type DEPS9601 and DEPS9601A
have been separately tested and certified by Nemko
(CBTC No. NO82590/A1/M2 and NO96755/M1) according
to IEC 60601-1:2005 +AMD1:2012, refer to attachment 5
and appended table 8.10.
The rechargeable Li-ion battery, type SDB-3S1PA has
been separately tested and certified by TÜV-Rh
(CBTC No. JPTUV-114329) according to
IEC 62133-2:2017, refer to attachment 6 and appended
table 8.10.
6 Classification The equipment has the following classifications:
- Type of protection against electric shock: Class I for
power supply box or Internally powered for digital flat
panel X-ray detector
- Degree of protection against electric shock (Patient
connections): Type B applied part for front panel of the
digital X-ray detector
- Degree of protection against harmful ingress of water or
particulate matter: Ordinary (IPX0)
- Methods of sterilization: The equipment is not intended to
be sterilized by user
- Degree of safety application for use in an oxygen
environment: Not applicable
- Mode of operation: Continuous operation with intermittent
loading

Clause Remarks Information/Comments
7 Identification, markings and
documents
Markings and instructions related to the safety shall be in a
language which is acceptable in the country in which the
equipment is to be sold. Markings and instructions in
English were evaluated in this test report.
7.1.1 and
12.2
Usability The equipment’s usability engineering process has been
evaluated according to IEC 60601-1-6. Refer to the
attachment 3, which incorporates the check list according to
IEC 62366.
8.6.4 Impedance and current-carrying
capability
Metal chassis of flat panel digital X-ray detector is
electrically connected to the protective earth terminal (earth
pin in the appliance inlet) of power supply box. However,
the impedance between earth pin of appliance inlet and
metal chassis of flat panel digital X-ray detector exceed
100 mΩ. Therefore, metal chassis and flat panel surface of
flat panel digital X-ray detector are considered as unearthed
metal enclosure in this test report, refer to insulation
diagram.
8.11.3 Power supply cord set Refer to the appended table 8.10, which is the list of
critical component parts. Power supply cord set for other
countries shall comply with the national regulations of the
country in which the equipment is to be sold.
14 Programmable electrical medical
systems (PEMS)
The software life-cycle process has been evaluated
according to IEC 60601-1, clause 14 and IEC 62304.
Compliance to the IEC 62304 is documented by the
manufacturer and reviewed by Nemko.
See “Attachment - Software” in this test report.
16 ME system This test report does not cover the clause 16. The
compliance shall be tested and evaluated in the end-
product (X-ray system including operating PC) when the
equipment constitutes as ME system with end-product.
Refer to general product information for set-up diagram and
further consideration.
17 Electromagnetic compatibility The manufacturer has declared that the equipment is in
compliance with the requirements of IEC 60601-1-2.
Compliance is documented by the manufacturer.

Calibration All instruments used in the tests given in this test report are calibrated and

Measurement
uncertainty
Measurement uncertainties are calculated for all instruments and instrument
set-ups given in this report. Calculations are based on the principles given in
the standard EA-4/02, IEC Guide 115:2007 and other relevant internal Nemko-
procedures.
Further information about measurement uncertainties will be given on request.
Evaluation of results If not explicitly stated otherwise in the standard, the test is passed if the
measured value is equal to or below (above) the limit line, regardless of the
measurement uncertainty. If the measured value is above (below) the limit line,
the test is not passed - ref IEC Guide 115:2007. The instrumentation accuracy is
within limits agreed by IECEE-CTL.

Page 15 of 170 Report No. 397950
TRF No. IEC60601_1P
General product information:
The equipment is intended to be indicated for digital imaging solution designed for providing general
radiographic diagnosis of human anatomy targeting both adult and children used in a hospital or other
institutional healthcare environment. It is intended to replace film based radiographic diagnostic systems and
provide more precise case diagnosis and treatment planning on a real time basis for physicians and
radiologists. But the equipment is not intended to be used for mammography and direct cardiac application.
The equipment consists of power supply box, digital flat panel X-ray detector, switch box and exposure
switch. The power supply box and digital flat panel X-ray detector are intended for use with patient

environment. The switch box and exposure switch are intended for use outside patient environment.
The digital flat panel X-ray detector is intended to be powered from the supply mains (via power supply box)
or internal electrical power source (rechargeable Li-ion battery). Therefore, the equipment is classified as
- Class I ME equipment when the power supply box is connected to the supply mains, or
- Internally powered ME equipment when the power box is disconnected to the supply mains
The equipment provides with battery recharger and its AC adapter which is intended to be powered from the
separate supply mains. These components are intended to be used outside patient environment and certified
according to IEC 60950-1. Therefore, these components are not tested and evaluated in this test report.
The equipment is generally used and installed in the end-product (X-ray system including operating PC).
Refer to set-up diagram which is intended by the manufacturer.
Based on above set-up diagram, further consideration shall be checked as following when the equipment is
installed in the end-product.
- The suitability of the mounting means shall be determined.
- The compliance shall be tested and evaluated when the equipment constitutes as ME system with
end-product.
- End- product (X-ray system) shall be powered from separate supply mains which complies with
IEC 60601-1.
- Operation PC shall be powered from separate supply mains which complies with IEC 60601-1 or
IEC 60950-1.
All testing was conducted with the PC submitted by manufacturer (Type: Latitude, manufactured by Dell Inc.)
as representative.

Supplementary Information:
1) Multiplication factor (1.14 for MOOP) is applied for altitude up to 3000 m based on table 8.
2) Highest working voltage is taken from the certified power supply box test report.
3) Measurements is transposed from the certified power supply box test report.
4) Short-circuit testing was considered due to the insufficient insulation distance. Leakage current testing
was performed during short-circuit in order to show not hazard in this area, refer to appended table 8.7.
INSULATION DIAGRAM CONVENTIONS and GUIDANCE:
A measured value must be provided in the value columns for the device under evaluation. The symbol >
(greater than sign) must not be used. Switch-mode power supplies must be re-evaluated in the device under
evaluation therefore N/A must not be used with a generic statement that the component is certified.
Insulation diagram is a graphical representation of equipment insulation barriers, protective impedance and
protective earthing. If feasible, use the following conventions to generate the diagram:
- All isolation barriers are identified by letters between separate parts of diagram, for example separate
transformer
windings, optocouplers, wire insulation, creepage and clearance distances.
- Parts connected to earth with large dots are protectively earthed. Other connections to earth are functional
- Applied parts are extended beyond the equipment enclosure and terminated with an arrow.
- Parts accessible to the operator only are extended outside of the enclosure but are not terminated with an
arrow.

4.3 [A, B, C] Software safety classification —
a) The MANUFACTURER assigned to each SOFTWARE
SYSTEM a software safety class (A, B, or C)
according to the possible effects on the patient,
operator, or other people resulting from a HAZARD to
which the SOFTWARE SYSTEM can contribute.
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 1 Level of concern
P
The software safety classes initially be assigned based on severity as follows: —
Class A: No injury or damage to health is possible N/A
Class B: Non-SERIOUS INJURY is possible Software Class: B P
Class C: Death or SERIOUS INJURY is possible N/A
If the HAZARD could arise from a failure of the
SOFTWARE SYSTEM to behave as specified, the
probability of such failure assumed to be 100 per
cent
P
If the RISK of non- SERIOUS INJURY arising from a
software failure is similarly reduced to an acceptable
level by a hardware RISK CONTROL measure, the
software safety classification may be reduced from
B to A.
P
b) The MANUFACTURER assigned to each SOFTWARE
SYSTEM that contributes to the implementation of a
RISK CONTROL measure a software safety class
based on the possible effects of the HAZARD that the
RISK CONTROL measure is controlling.
P
c) The MANUFACTURER documented the software
safety class assigned to each SOFTWARE SYSTEM in
the RISK MANAGEMENT FILE
P
d) When a SOFTWARE SYSTEM is decomposed into
SOFTWARE ITEMS, and when a SOFTWARE ITEM is
decomposed into further SOFTWARE ITEMS, such
SOFTWARE ITEMS inherited the software safety
classification of the original SOFTWARE ITEM (or
SOFTWARE SYSTEM) unless the MANUFACTURER
documents a rationale for classification into a
different software safety class.
P
A rationale explained how the new SOFTWARE ITEMS
are segregated so that they may be classified
separately
P
e) The MANUFACTURER documented the software
safety class of each SOFTWARE ITEM if that class is
different from the class of the SOFTWARE ITEM from
which it was created by decomposition
P

Page 155 of 170 Report No. 397950
IEC 60601-1
Clause Requirement + Test Result - Remark Verdict
TRF No. IEC60601_1P
Attachment - Software – IEC 62304:2006 —
f) Wherever a PROCESS is required for SOFTWARE
ITEMS of a specific classification and the PROCESS is
necessarily applied to a group of SOFTWARE ITEMS,
the MANUFACTURER used the PROCESSES and TASKS
which are required by the classification of the
highest-classified SOFTWARE ITEM in the group
unless the MANUFACTURER documents in the RISK
MANAGEMENT FILE a rationale for using a lower
classification
P
g) For each SOFTWARE SYSTEM, until a software
safety class is assigned, Class C requirements
applied.
N/A

7 SOFTWARE RISK MANAGEMENT PROCESS —
7.1 Analysis of software contributing to hazardous situations —
7.1.1 [B, C] The MANUFACTURER identifies SOFTWARE ITEMS
that could contribute to a hazardous situation
identified in the MEDICAL DEVICE RISK ANALYSIS
ACTIVITY of ISO 14971
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 10 Hazard analysis
P
7.1.2 [B, C] The MANUFACTURER identifies potential causes
of the SOFTWARE ITEM identified above contributing
to a hazardous situation
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 10 Hazard analysis
P
The MANUFACTURER considers potential causes including, as appropriate: P
a) incorrect or incomplete specification of
functionality
P
b) software defects in the identified SOFTWARE ITEM
functionality
P
c) failure or unexpected results from SOUP N/A
d) hardware failures or other software defects that
could result in unpredictable software operation
P
e) reasonably foreseeable misuse P
7.1.3 [B, C] If failure or unexpected results from SOUP is a
potential cause of the SOFTWARE ITEM contributing to
a hazardous situation, the MANUFACTURER
EVALUATED as a minimum any ANOMALY list
published by the supplier of the SOUP item relevant
to the VERSION of the SOUP item used in the MEDICAL
DEVICE to determine if any of the known ANOMALIES
result in a sequence of events that could result in a
hazardous situation
N/A
7.1.4 [B, C] The MANUFACTURER documents in the RISK
MANAGEMENT FILE potential causes of the SOFTWARE
ITEM contributing to a hazardous situation
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 10 Hazard analysis
P

[B, C] The MANUFACTURER documented in the RISK
MANAGEMENT FILE sequences of events that could
result in a hazardous situation that are identified in
7.1.2
P
7.2 RISK CONTROL measures —
7.2.1 [B, C] For each potential cause of the software item

and documented risk control measures

(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 10 Hazard analysis
P

SOFTWARE ITEM, the MANUFACTURER:
P
a) includes the RISK CONTROL measure in the
software requirements
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 10 Hazard analysis
P
b) assign a software safety class to the SOFTWARE
ITEM based on the possible effects of the HAZARD
that the RISK CONTROL measure is controlling
P
c) develops the SOFTWARE ITEM in accordance with
Clause 5
P
7.3 VERIFICATION of RISK CONTROL measures —
7.3.1 [B, C] The implementation of each RISK CONTROL
measure documented in 7.2 is VERIFIED, and this
VERIFICATION is documented
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 10 Hazard analysis
P
7.3.2 [B, C] If a RISK CONTROL measure is implemented as

a SOFTWARE ITEM, the MANUFACTURER EVALUATED the
RISK CONTROL measure to identify and document in
the RISK MANAGEMENT FILE any new sequences of
events that could result in a hazardous situation
P
7.3.3 [B, C] The MANUFACTURER documents TRACEABILITY of software HAZARDS as
appropriate:
P
a) from the hazardous situation to the SOFTWARE
ITEM
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-046, Rev. 0)
- 10 Hazard analysis
P
b) from the SOFTWARE ITEM to the specific software
cause
P
c) from the software cause to the RISK CONTROL
measure
P
d) from the RISK CONTROL measure to the
VERIFICATION of the RISK CONTROL measure
P
